</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L36" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="36"></td>
        <td id="LC36" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>I assume that the contributors would agree with me that this handbook is probably the wrong place to go into great technical detail on mathematical or computational subjects, but there needs to be at least something there to serve as a starting point from which the reader could choose to jump into some of the papers cited.‚Äé A summary of the major trends and the high-level intuitions behind a lot of the technical terminology that readers will encounter in HPSG-related CL papers, for example, would both be most welcome.</span></td>

        <td id="L38" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="38"></td>
        <td id="LC38" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Introduction}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L39" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="39"></td>
        <td id="LC39" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L40" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="40"></td>
        <td id="LC40" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> First draft: Emily</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L41" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="41"></td>
        <td id="LC41" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L42" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="42"></td>
        <td id="LC42" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">From the inception of HPSG in the 1980s,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L43" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="43"></td>
        <td id="LC43" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">there has been a close integration between theoretical and computational work</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L44" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="44"></td>
        <td id="LC44" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\crossrefchapterp</span>[for an overview, see]{evolution}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L45" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="45"></td>
        <td id="LC45" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span>\citep{FIXME-CLobit-or-other}.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L46" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="46"></td>
        <td id="LC46" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> at HP Labs in the joint work of Ivan Sag, Geoff Pullum, Tom Wasow, Mark Gawron, Carl Pollard and Dan Flickinger</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L47" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="47"></td>
        <td id="LC47" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> GE: I think this list of authors is too long for a first sentence.  Do we need to do more than refer to the other chapter?</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L48" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="48"></td>
        <td id="LC48" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2018-09-28 sounds good!</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L49" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="49"></td>
        <td id="LC49" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In this chapter, we discuss computational work in HPSG,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L50" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="50"></td>
        <td id="LC50" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">starting with the infrastructure that supports it (both theoretical and practical) in Section~<span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{cl:infrastructure}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L51" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="51"></td>
        <td id="LC51" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Next we describe several existing large-scale projects which build HPSG or HPSG-inspired grammars</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L52" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="52"></td>
        <td id="LC52" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(see Section~<span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{cl:resources})</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L53" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="53"></td>
        <td id="LC53" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and the deployment of such grammars in applications including both those within linguistic research and otherwise</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L54" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="54"></td>
        <td id="LC54" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(see Section~<span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{cl:deployment}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L55" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="55"></td>
        <td id="LC55" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Finally, we turn to linguistic insights gleaned from broad-coverage grammar development</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L56" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="56"></td>
        <td id="LC56" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(see Section~<span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{cl:insight}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L57" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="57"></td>
        <td id="LC57" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L58" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="58"></td>
        <td id="LC58" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2018-07-26 That seems like a relatively weak intro, but putting it in as a place-holder for now. </span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L59" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="59"></td>
        <td id="LC59" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L60" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="60"></td>
        <td id="LC60" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2018-07-26 Also, I wonder if ``lessons for linguistics&#39;&#39; might not come across as condescending...</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L61" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="61"></td>
        <td id="LC61" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> GE 2018-07-31 Yes, maybe best to reword that somehow... ``Linguistic insights&#39;&#39;?</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L62" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="62"></td>
        <td id="LC62" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2018-09-28 Thanks.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L63" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="63"></td>
        <td id="LC63" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L64" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="64"></td>
        <td id="LC64" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Infrastructure}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L65" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="65"></td>
        <td id="LC65" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{cl:infrastructure}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L66" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="66"></td>
        <td id="LC66" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L67" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="67"></td>
        <td id="LC67" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Theoretical considerations}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L68" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="68"></td>
        <td id="LC68" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{cl:theoretical}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L69" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="69"></td>
        <td id="LC69" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L70" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="70"></td>
        <td id="LC70" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There are several properties of HPSG as a theory that make it well-suited to computational implementation.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L71" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="71"></td>
        <td id="LC71" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">First, the theory is kept separate from the formalism:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L72" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="72"></td>
        <td id="LC72" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the formalism is expressive enough to encode a wide variety of possible theories.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L73" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="73"></td>
        <td id="LC73" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">While some theoretical work does argue for or against the necessity of particular formal devices</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L74" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="74"></td>
        <td id="LC74" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(<span class="pl-c1">\eg</span><span class="pl-cce">\ </span>the shuffle operator <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{Reape94a}),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L75" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="75"></td>
        <td id="LC75" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">much of it proceeds within shared assumptions about the formalism.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L76" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="76"></td>
        <td id="LC76" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is in contrast to work in the context of the Minimalist Program <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{Chomsky93b-u},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L77" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="77"></td>
        <td id="LC77" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where theoretical results are typically couched in terms of modifications to the formalism itself.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L78" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="78"></td>
        <td id="LC78" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">From a computational point of view, the benefit of differentiating between theory and formalism</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L79" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="79"></td>
        <td id="LC79" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">is that the formalism is relatively stable.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L80" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="80"></td>
        <td id="LC80" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">That enables the development and maintenance of software systems that target the formalism <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{boguraev1988software},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L81" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="81"></td>
        <td id="LC81" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">such as software for parsing, generation, and grammar exploration</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L82" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="82"></td>
        <td id="LC82" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(see Section~<span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{cl:resources} below for some examples).<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L83" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="83"></td>
        <td id="LC83" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	There are implementations of Minimalism, notably <span class="pl-c1">\citealt</span>{Stabler97a-u} and <span class="pl-c1">\citealt</span>{Herring:16}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L84" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="84"></td>
        <td id="LC84" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	However, implementing a theory requires fixing the formalism,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L85" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="85"></td>
        <td id="LC85" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	and so these implementations are unlikely to be useful for testing theoretical ideas as the theory moves on.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L86" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="86"></td>
        <td id="LC86" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L87" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="87"></td>
        <td id="LC87" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L88" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="88"></td>
        <td id="LC88" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A second important property of HPSG that supports a strong connection between theoretical and computational work is an interest in both so-called `core&#39; and so-called `peripheral&#39; phenomena. Most implemented grammars are built with the goal of handling naturally occurring text.<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{It is possible, but less common, to do implementation work strictly against test suites of sentences constructed specifically to focus on phenomena of interest.} This means that they will need to handle a wide variety of linguistic phenomena not always treated in theoretical syntactic work <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{Baldwin-et-al-05}. A syntactic framework that excludes research on `peripheral&#39; phenomena as uninteresting provides less support for implementational work than does one, like HPSG or Construction Grammar, that values such topics</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L89" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="89"></td>
        <td id="LC89" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\crossrefchapterp</span>[for a comparison of HPSG and Construction Grammar, see]{cxg}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L90" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="90"></td>
        <td id="LC90" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L91" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="91"></td>
        <td id="LC91" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Finally, the type hierarchy characteristic of HPSG lends itself well to developing broad-coverage grammars which are maintainable over time (see \citealt{Syg:Win:11}). The use of the type hierarchy to manage complexity at scale comes out of the work of \citet{Flickinger87} and others at HP labs in the project where HPSG was originally developed. The core idea is that any given constraint is (ideally) expressed only once on types which serve as supertypes to all entities that bear that constraint.\footnote{Originally this only applied to lexical entries in Flickinger&#39;s work. Now it also applies phrase structure rules, lexical rules, and types below the level of the sign which are used in the definition of all of these.} Such constraints might represent broad generalizations that apply to many entities or relatively narrow, idiosyncratic properties that apply to only a few. By isolating any given constraint on one type (as opposed to repeating it in mutiple places), we build grammars that are easier to update and adapt in light of new data that require refinements to constraints. Having a single locus for each constraint also makes the types a very useful target for documentation \citep{Hashimoto-etal:07} and grammar exploration \citep{Letcher:18}. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L92" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="92"></td>
        <td id="LC92" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L93" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="93"></td>
        <td id="LC93" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L94" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="94"></td>
        <td id="LC94" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Practical considerations}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L95" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="95"></td>
        <td id="LC95" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{cl:prac}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L96" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="96"></td>
        <td id="LC96" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L97" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="97"></td>
        <td id="LC97" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">HPSG allows practical implementations,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L98" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="98"></td>
        <td id="LC98" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">because it uses a well-defined formalism.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L99" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="99"></td>
        <td id="LC99" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Furthermore, because HPSG is defined to be bi-directional,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L100" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="100"></td>
        <td id="LC100" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">an implemented grammar can be used for both parsing and generation.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L101" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="101"></td>
        <td id="LC101" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In this section, we discuss how HPSG allows tractable algorithms,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L102" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="102"></td>
        <td id="LC102" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which enables linguists to empirically test hypotheses,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L103" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="103"></td>
        <td id="LC103" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and which also enables HPSG grammars to be used in a range of applications,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L104" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="104"></td>
        <td id="LC104" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">as we will see in Sections~<span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{cl:lang-doc} and~<span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{cl:downstream}, respectively.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L105" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="105"></td>
        <td id="LC105" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L106" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="106"></td>
        <td id="LC106" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsubsection</span>{Computational complexity}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L107" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="107"></td>
        <td id="LC107" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{cl:prac:comp}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L108" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="108"></td>
        <td id="LC108" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L109" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="109"></td>
        <td id="LC109" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One way to measure how easy or difficult it is</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L110" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="110"></td>
        <td id="LC110" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">to use a syntactic theory in practical computational applications</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L111" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="111"></td>
        <td id="LC111" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">is to consider the <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{computational complexity}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L112" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="112"></td>
        <td id="LC112" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">of parsing and generation algorithms <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{gazdar1985complexity}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L113" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="113"></td>
        <td id="LC113" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Computational complexity in this case includes both how much</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L114" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="114"></td>
        <td id="LC114" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">memory and how much computational time </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L115" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="115"></td>
        <td id="LC115" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">a parsing algorithm needs to process a particular sentence.<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> </span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L116" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="116"></td>
        <td id="LC116" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  In this section, we only consider parsing</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L117" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="117"></td>
        <td id="LC117" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  algorithms, but a similar analysis can be done for generation</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L118" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="118"></td>
        <td id="LC118" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>[<span class="pl-c1">\eg</span>][]{carroll1999generate}.}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L119" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="119"></td>
        <td id="LC119" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Considering parsing time, longer sentences should always take longer to process,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L120" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="120"></td>
        <td id="LC120" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">but the more complex the algorithm is,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L121" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="121"></td>
        <td id="LC121" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the more quickly the amount of processing time increases.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L122" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="122"></td>
        <td id="LC122" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Parsing complexity can thus be measured by considering sentences containing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>~tokens,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L123" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="123"></td>
        <td id="LC123" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">finding the average amount of time taken or the longest amount of time taken,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L124" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="124"></td>
        <td id="LC124" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and then increasing~<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to see how the amount of time changes.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L125" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="125"></td>
        <td id="LC125" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2019-02-21 Edits just above to work around pedantic mathy `we&#39;.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L126" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="126"></td>
        <td id="LC126" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> GE 2019-02-25 (Reply via email).</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L127" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="127"></td>
        <td id="LC127" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L128" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="128"></td>
        <td id="LC128" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">At first sight, analysing computational complexity</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L129" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="129"></td>
        <td id="LC129" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">would seem to paint HPSG in a bad light,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L130" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="130"></td>
        <td id="LC130" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">because the formalism allows us to write grammars</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L131" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="131"></td>
        <td id="LC131" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which can be arbitrarily complex;</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L132" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="132"></td>
        <td id="LC132" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">in technical terminology, the formalism is <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{Turing-complete}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L133" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="133"></td>
        <td id="LC133" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>[Section~3.4]{Johnson88}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L134" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="134"></td>
        <td id="LC134" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> maybe also relevant:</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L135" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="135"></td>
        <td id="LC135" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> Barton, Berwick, Ristad (1987)</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L136" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="136"></td>
        <td id="LC136" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> ``Computational Complexity and Natural Language&#39;&#39;</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L137" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="137"></td>
        <td id="LC137" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">However, as discussed in the previous section,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L138" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="138"></td>
        <td id="LC138" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">there is a clear distinction between theory and formalism.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L139" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="139"></td>
        <td id="LC139" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Although the HPSG formalism rules out the possibility of efficient algorithms</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L140" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="140"></td>
        <td id="LC140" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">that could cope with any possible feature-structure grammar,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L141" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="141"></td>
        <td id="LC141" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">a particular theory (or a particular grammar) might well allow efficient algorithms.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L142" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="142"></td>
        <td id="LC142" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L143" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="143"></td>
        <td id="LC143" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Keeping processing complexity manageable is handled differently</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L144" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="144"></td>
        <td id="LC144" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">in other computationally-friendly frameworks,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L145" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="145"></td>
        <td id="LC145" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">such as Combinatory Categorial Grammar (CCG),<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L146" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="146"></td>
        <td id="LC146" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	For an introduction, see <span class="pl-c1">\citet</span>{steedman2011ccg}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L147" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="147"></td>
        <td id="LC147" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	For a comparison with HPSG, see <span class="pl-c1">\crossrefchaptert</span>{cg}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L148" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="148"></td>
        <td id="LC148" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L149" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="149"></td>
        <td id="LC149" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">or Tree Adjoining Grammar <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>[TAG;][]{Joshi87a-u,SAJ88a-u}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L150" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="150"></td>
        <td id="LC150" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The formalisms of CCG and TAG inherently limit computational complexity:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L151" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="151"></td>
        <td id="LC151" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">for both of them, as the sentence length~<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> increases,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L152" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="152"></td>
        <td id="LC152" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">worst-case parsing time is proportional to~<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n^<span class="pl-c1">6</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{Kasamietal1989}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L153" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="153"></td>
        <td id="LC153" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is a deliberate feature of these formalisms,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L154" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="154"></td>
        <td id="LC154" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which aim to be just expressive enough to capture human language,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L155" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="155"></td>
        <td id="LC155" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and not any more expressive.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L156" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="156"></td>
        <td id="LC156" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Building this kind of constraint into the formalism itself</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L157" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="157"></td>
        <td id="LC157" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">highlights a different school of thought from HPSG.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L158" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="158"></td>
        <td id="LC158" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Indeed, <span class="pl-c1">\citet</span>{MuellerCoreGram} explicitly argues</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L159" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="159"></td>
        <td id="LC159" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">in favor of developing linguistic analyses first,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L160" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="160"></td>
        <td id="LC160" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and improving processing efficiency second.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L161" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="161"></td>
        <td id="LC161" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">As discussed above in Section~<span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{cl:theoretical},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L162" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="162"></td>
        <td id="LC162" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">separating the formalism from the theory</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L163" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="163"></td>
        <td id="LC163" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">means that the formalism is stable, even as the theory develops.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L164" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="164"></td>
        <td id="LC164" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L165" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="165"></td>
        <td id="LC165" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2018-09-28 Say something here about particular analytical choices that constrain the processing complexity? (The bit about the fact that the lists that we read from tend to be limited in length.)</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L166" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="166"></td>
        <td id="LC166" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> GE 2019-02-05 The length of the lists might be a red herring,</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L167" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="167"></td>
        <td id="LC167" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> because apart from the items on the hook, the other elements don&#39;t affect grammaticality.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L168" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="168"></td>
        <td id="LC168" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> Potentially relevant for the size of $C$ below, but I worry this would be too much detail.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L169" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="169"></td>
        <td id="LC169" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2018-09-28 Maybe also cite Flickinger 2000 (`On building a more efficient grammar using types&#39;) and Copestake et al work on improving generator efficiency.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L170" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="170"></td>
        <td id="LC170" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> GE 2019-02-05 Thanks, updated.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L171" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="171"></td>
        <td id="LC171" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L172" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="172"></td>
        <td id="LC172" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">It would be beyond the scope of this chapter</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L173" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="173"></td>
        <td id="LC173" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">to give a full review of parsing algorithms,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L174" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="174"></td>
        <td id="LC174" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">but it is instructive to give an example.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L175" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="175"></td>
        <td id="LC175" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For grammars that have a context-free backbone</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L176" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="176"></td>
        <td id="LC176" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(every derivation can be expressed as a phrase-structure tree</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L177" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="177"></td>
        <td id="LC177" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">plus constraints between mother and daughter nodes),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L178" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="178"></td>
        <td id="LC178" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">it is possible to adapt the standard <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{chart-parsing} algorithm <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{kay:1973} for context-free grammars.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L179" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="179"></td>
        <td id="LC179" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2019-02-21 We should have cite for chart-parsing. It looks like Kay 1973 is the originator of that idea, so putting that in for now.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L180" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="180"></td>
        <td id="LC180" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The basic idea is to parse ``bottom-up&#39;&#39;,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L181" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="181"></td>
        <td id="LC181" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">starting by finding analyses for each token in the input,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L182" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="182"></td>
        <td id="LC182" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and then finding analyses for increasingly longer sequences of tokens (called <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{spans},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L183" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="183"></td>
        <td id="LC183" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">until the parser reaches the entire sentence.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L184" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="184"></td>
        <td id="LC184" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L185" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="185"></td>
        <td id="LC185" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For a context-free grammar, there is a finite number of nonterminal symbols,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L186" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="186"></td>
        <td id="LC186" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and each span is analysed as a subset of the nonterminals.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L187" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="187"></td>
        <td id="LC187" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For a feature-structure grammar, each span must be analysed as a set of feature structures,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L188" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="188"></td>
        <td id="LC188" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which makes the algorithm more complicated.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L189" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="189"></td>
        <td id="LC189" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In principle, a grammar may allow an infinite number of possible feature structures,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L190" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="190"></td>
        <td id="LC190" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">for example if it includes recursive unary rules.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L191" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="191"></td>
        <td id="LC191" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">However, if we can bound the number of possible feature structures as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L192" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="192"></td>
        <td id="LC192" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">then the worst-case parsing time is proportional to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> n^{<span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>+1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L193" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="193"></td>
        <td id="LC193" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\rho</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the maximum number of children in a phrase-structure rule</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L194" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="194"></td>
        <td id="LC194" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>[Section~3.2.3]{carroll1993parse}. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L195" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="195"></td>
        <td id="LC195" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is less complex than for an arbitrary grammar</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L196" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="196"></td>
        <td id="LC196" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(which means that this class of grammars is <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{not} Turing-complete),</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L217" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="217"></td>

        <td id="LC218" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">recursion in feature paths (<span class="pl-c1">\eg</span><span class="pl-cce">\ </span>the elements on the <span class="pl-c1">\textsc</span>{comps}</td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L221" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="221"></td>

      </tr>

        <td id="L222" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="222"></td>

      </tr>

      <tr>
        <td id="L276" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="276"></td>
        <td id="LC276" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A well-constructed grammar should be expected to return multiple</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L277" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="277"></td>
        <td id="LC277" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">parses for each ambiguous sentence.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L278" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="278"></td>
        <td id="LC278" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L279" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="279"></td>
        <td id="LC279" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">However, people are naturally very good at resolving ambiguity,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L280" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="280"></td>
        <td id="LC280" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which means most ambiguity is not apparent, even to linguists.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L281" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="281"></td>
        <td id="LC281" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">It is only with the development of large-scale grammars that the sheer scale of ambiguity has become clear.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L282" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="282"></td>
        <td id="LC282" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2018-10-03 What&#39;s rref?</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L283" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="283"></td>
        <td id="LC283" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> GE 2018-11-27 an example in brackets (from localcommands.tex)</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L284" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="284"></td>
        <td id="LC284" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> (normally, I&#39;d prefer \cref from cleveref, but we don&#39;t seem to be using that for this handbook)</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L285" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="285"></td>
        <td id="LC285" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For example, <span class="pl-c1">\rref</span>{cl:ex:ambig-simple}~might seem unambiguous,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L286" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="286"></td>
        <td id="LC286" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">but there is a second reading, where <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{my favorite} is the topicalized object of <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{speak},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L287" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="287"></td>
        <td id="LC287" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which would mean that town criers generally speak the speaker&#39;s favorite thing (perhaps a language) clearly.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L288" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="288"></td>
        <td id="LC288" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There is also a third, even more implausible reading, where <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{my favorite town} is the topicalized object.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L289" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="289"></td>
        <td id="LC289" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Such implausible readings don&#39;t easily come to mind,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L290" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="290"></td>
        <td id="LC290" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and in fact, the 2018 version of the English Resource Grammar <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>[ERG;][]{Flickinger2000a,Flickinger2011a-u}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L291" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="291"></td>
        <td id="LC291" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">gives a total of 21 readings for this sentence.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L292" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="292"></td>
        <td id="LC292" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">With increasingly long sentences, such ambiguities stack up very quickly.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L293" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="293"></td>
        <td id="LC293" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For~<span class="pl-c1">\rref</span>{cl:ex:ambig-many}, the first line of a newspaper article,<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L294" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="294"></td>
        <td id="LC294" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	<span class="pl-c1">\url</span>{https://www.theguardian.com/science/2018/aug/22/offspring-of-neanderthal-and-denisovan-identified-for-first-time}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L295" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="295"></td>
        <td id="LC295" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L296" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="296"></td>
        <td id="LC296" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the ERG gives 35,094 readings.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L297" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="297"></td>
        <td id="LC297" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L298" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="298"></td>
        <td id="LC298" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{exe}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L299" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="299"></td>
        <td id="LC299" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\ex\label</span>{cl:ex:ambig-simple}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L300" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="300"></td>
        <td id="LC300" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">My favorite town criers speak clearly.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L301" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="301"></td>
        <td id="LC301" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\ex\label</span>{cl:ex:ambig-many}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L302" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="302"></td>
        <td id="LC302" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A small piece of bone found in a cave in Siberia has been identified</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L303" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="303"></td>
        <td id="LC303" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">as the remnant of a child whose mother was a Neanderthal and father was a Denisovan,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L304" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="304"></td>
        <td id="LC304" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">a mysterious human ancestor that lived in the region.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L305" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="305"></td>
        <td id="LC305" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{exe}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L306" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="306"></td>
        <td id="LC306" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L307" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="307"></td>
        <td id="LC307" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2018-09-28 Editing a bit through here:</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L308" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="308"></td>
        <td id="LC308" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> GE thanks!</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L309" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="309"></td>
        <td id="LC309" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">While exploring ambiguity can be interesting for a linguist,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L310" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="310"></td>
        <td id="LC310" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">typical practical applications require just one parse per input sentence</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L311" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="311"></td>
        <td id="LC311" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and specifically the parse that best reflects the intended meaning</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L312" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="312"></td>
        <td id="LC312" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(or only the top few parses, in case the one put forward as `best&#39; might be wrong).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L313" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="313"></td>
        <td id="LC313" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Thus, what is required is a <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{ranking} of the parses,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L314" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="314"></td>
        <td id="LC314" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">so that the application can only use the most highly-ranked parse,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L315" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="315"></td>
        <td id="LC315" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">or the top~<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>N<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> parses.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L316" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="316"></td>
        <td id="LC316" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L317" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="317"></td>
        <td id="LC317" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Parse ranking is not usually determined by the grammar itself, because</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L318" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="318"></td>
        <td id="LC318" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">of the difficulty of manually writing disambiguation</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L319" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="319"></td>
        <td id="LC319" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">rules.<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{In fact, in earlier work, this task was undertaken by</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L320" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="320"></td>
        <td id="LC320" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  hand. One of the authors (Bender) had the job of maintaining rule</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L321" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="321"></td>
        <td id="LC321" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  weights in addition to developing the Jacy grammar <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{SBB2016a}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L322" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="322"></td>
        <td id="LC322" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  at YY Technologies in 2001--2002. No systematic methodology for</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L323" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="323"></td>
        <td id="LC323" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  determining appropriate weights was available and the system was</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L324" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="324"></td>
        <td id="LC324" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  both extremely brittle (sensitive to any changes in the grammar) and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L325" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="325"></td>
        <td id="LC325" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  next to impossible to maintain.}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L326" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="326"></td>
        <td id="LC326" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2019-02-21 Added the above footnote. TMI or fun historical detail?</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L327" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="327"></td>
        <td id="LC327" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> GE 2019-02-25 fun historical detail! I didn&#39;t know if there was anything to cite.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L328" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="328"></td>
        <td id="LC328" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Typically, a statistical system is used <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{Tou:Man:Shi:Fli:Oep:02,Tou:Man:Fli:Oep:05}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L329" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="329"></td>
        <td id="LC329" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">First, a corpus is <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{treebanked}:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L330" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="330"></td>
        <td id="LC330" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">for each sentence in the corpus,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L331" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="331"></td>
        <td id="LC331" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">an annotator (often the grammar writer) chooses the best parse,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L332" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="332"></td>
        <td id="LC332" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">out of all parses produced by the grammar.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L333" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="333"></td>
        <td id="LC333" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The set of all parses for a sentence is often referred to as the <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{parse forest},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L334" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="334"></td>
        <td id="LC334" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and the selected best parse is often referred to as the <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{gold standard}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L335" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="335"></td>
        <td id="LC335" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Given the gold parses for the whole corpus, a statistical system is trained</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L336" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="336"></td>
        <td id="LC336" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">to predict the gold parse from a parse forest,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L337" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="337"></td>
        <td id="LC337" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">based on many features<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L338" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="338"></td>
        <td id="LC338" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	In the machine-learning sense of ``feature&#39;&#39;,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L339" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="339"></td>
        <td id="LC339" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	not the feature-structure sense.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L340" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="340"></td>
        <td id="LC340" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L341" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="341"></td>
        <td id="LC341" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">of the parse.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L342" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="342"></td>
        <td id="LC342" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">From the example in~<span class="pl-c1">\rref</span>{cl:ex:ambig-simple},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L343" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="343"></td>
        <td id="LC343" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">a number of a different features all influence the preferred interpretation:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L344" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="344"></td>
        <td id="LC344" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the likelihood of a construction (such as topicalization),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L345" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="345"></td>
        <td id="LC345" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the likelihood of a valence frame (such as transitive <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{speak}),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L346" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="346"></td>
        <td id="LC346" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the likelihood of a collocation (such as <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{town crier}),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L347" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="347"></td>
        <td id="LC347" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the likelihood of a semantic relation (such as speaking a town),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L348" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="348"></td>
        <td id="LC348" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and so on.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L349" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="349"></td>
        <td id="LC349" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> GE 2019-02-05:</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L350" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="350"></td>
        <td id="LC350" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> - any more detail for MaxEnt parse ranking?</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L351" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="351"></td>
        <td id="LC351" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> - any other references?</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L352" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="352"></td>
        <td id="LC352" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L353" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="353"></td>
        <td id="LC353" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Because of the large number of possible parses,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L354" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="354"></td>
        <td id="LC354" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">it can be helpful to <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{prune} the search space:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L355" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="355"></td>
        <td id="LC355" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">rather than ranking the full set of parses,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L356" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="356"></td>
        <td id="LC356" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">ranking is restricted to a smaller set of parses.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L357" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="357"></td>
        <td id="LC357" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Carefully choosing how to restrict the parser&#39;s attention </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L358" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="358"></td>
        <td id="LC358" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">can drastically reduce processing time without hurting parsing accuracy,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L359" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="359"></td>
        <td id="LC359" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">as long as that the algorithm for selecting the subset</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L360" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="360"></td>
        <td id="LC360" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">includes the correct parse sufficiently frequently.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L361" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="361"></td>
        <td id="LC361" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One method, called <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{supertagging},<span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L362" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="362"></td>
        <td id="LC362" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	The term <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{supertagging}, due to <span class="pl-c1">\citet</span>{bangalore1999supertag},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L363" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="363"></td>
        <td id="LC363" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	refers to <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{part-of-speech tagging},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L364" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="364"></td>
        <td id="LC364" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	which predicts a part-of-speech for each input token,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L365" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="365"></td>
        <td id="LC365" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	from a relatively small set of part-of-speech tags.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L366" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="366"></td>
        <td id="LC366" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	Supertagging is ``super&#39;&#39;, in that it predicts detailed lexical entries,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L367" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="367"></td>
        <td id="LC367" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">	rather than simple parts of speech.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L368" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="368"></td>
        <td id="LC368" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L369" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="369"></td>
        <td id="LC369" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">exploits the fact that HPSG is a lexicalized theory:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L370" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="370"></td>
        <td id="LC370" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">choosing the correct lexical entry brings in rich information</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L371" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="371"></td>
        <td id="LC371" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">that can be exploited to rule out many possible parses.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L372" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="372"></td>
        <td id="LC372" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Thus if the correct lexical entry can be chosen prior to parsing</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L373" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="373"></td>
        <td id="LC373" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(<span class="pl-c1">\eg</span><span class="pl-cce">\ </span>on the basis of the prior and following words),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L374" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="374"></td>
        <td id="LC374" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the range of possible analyses the parser must consider is drastically reduced.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L375" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="375"></td>
        <td id="LC375" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Although there is a chance that the supertagger will predict the wrong lexical entry,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L376" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="376"></td>
        <td id="LC376" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">using a supertagger can often improve parsing accuracy,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L377" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="377"></td>
        <td id="LC377" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">by ruling out parses that the parse-ranking model might incorrectly rank too high.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L378" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="378"></td>
        <td id="LC378" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Supertagging was first applied to HPSG by <span class="pl-c1">\citet</span>{matsuzaki2007supertag},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L379" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="379"></td>
        <td id="LC379" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">building on previous work for TAG <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{bangalore1999supertag}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L380" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="380"></td>
        <td id="LC380" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and CCG <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{clark2004supertag}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L381" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="381"></td>
        <td id="LC381" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">To allow multi-word expressions (such as <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{by and large}),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L382" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="382"></td>
        <td id="LC382" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where the grammar assigns a single lexical entry to multiple tokens,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L383" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="383"></td>
        <td id="LC383" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\citet</span>{dridan2013ubertag} proposes an extension of supertagging, called <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{ubertagging},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L384" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="384"></td>
        <td id="LC384" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which jointly predicts both a segmentation of the input and supertags for those segments.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L385" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="385"></td>
        <td id="LC385" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\citeauthor</span>{dridan2013ubertag} manages to increase parsing speed by a factor of four,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L386" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="386"></td>
        <td id="LC386" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">while also improving parsing accuracy.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L387" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="387"></td>
        <td id="LC387" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> Pruning via chunking? Muszy≈Ñska http://aclweb.org/anthology/P16-3014</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L388" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="388"></td>
        <td id="LC388" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L389" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="389"></td>
        <td id="LC389" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> EMB 2018-09-28 Doesn&#39;t Bec also bring in the lexical rules? Maybe that&#39;s too much detail for here.</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L390" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="390"></td>
        <td id="LC390" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L391" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="391"></td>
        <td id="LC391" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Finally, in order to train these statistical systems,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L392" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="392"></td>
        <td id="LC392" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">we need to first annotate a treebank.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L393" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="393"></td>
        <td id="LC393" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">When there are many parses for a sentence,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L394" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="394"></td>
        <td id="LC394" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">it can be time-consuming to select the best parse.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L395" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="395"></td>
        <td id="LC395" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">To efficiently use an annotator&#39;s time,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L396" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="396"></td>
        <td id="LC396" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">it can be helpful to use <span class="pl-c1">\textit</span>{discriminants},</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L397" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="397"></td>
        <td id="LC397" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">properties which hold for some parses but not for others <span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{Carter:97}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L398" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="398"></td>
        <td id="LC398" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For example, discriminants might include</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L399" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="399"></td>
        <td id="LC399" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">whether to analyse an ambiguous token as a noun or a verb,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L400" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="400"></td>
        <td id="LC400" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">or where to attach a prepositional phrase.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L401" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="401"></td>
        <td id="LC401" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This approach to treebanking also means that</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L402" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="402"></td>
        <td id="LC402" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">annotations can be re-used when the grammar is updated</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L403" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="403"></td>
        <td id="LC403" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\citep</span>{OFTM2004a-u,Fli:Oep:Ben:17}. For more on treebanking, see Section~<span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{cl:lang-doc:treebanks}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L404" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="404"></td>
        <td id="LC404" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L405" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="405"></td>
        <td id="LC405" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">%</span> Self-training?</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L406" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="406"></td>
